    31→
    32→type Sample struct {
    33→	T time.Time
    34→	V string
    35→}
    36→
    37→func (r Sample) MarshalJSON() ([]byte, error) {
    38→	return json.Marshal([2]string{
    39→		fmt.Sprintf("%d", r.T.UnixNano()), r.V,
    40→	})
    41→}
    42→
    43→func (r *Sample) UnmarshalJSON(b []byte) error {
    44→	var tuple [2]string
    45→	if err := json.Unmarshal(b, &tuple); err != nil {
    46→		return fmt.Errorf("failed to deserialize sample in Loki response: %w", err)
    47→	}
    48→	nano, err := strconv.ParseInt(tuple[0], 10, 64)
    49→	if err != nil {
    50→		return fmt.Errorf("timestamp in Loki sample not convertible to nanosecond epoch: %v", tuple[0])
    51→	}
    52→	r.T = time.Unix(0, nano)
    53→	r.V = tuple[1]
    54→	return nil
    55→}

    46→func makeDataRequest(ctx context.Context, lokiDsUrl string, query lokiQuery) (*http.Request, error) {
    47→	qs := url.Values{}
    48→	qs.Set("query", query.Expr)
    49→
    50→	qs.Set("direction", string(query.Direction))
    51→
    52→	// MaxLines defaults to zero when not received,
    53→	// and Loki does not like limit=0, even when it is not needed
    54→	// (for example for metric queries), so we
    55→	// only send it when it's set
    56→	if query.MaxLines > 0 {
    57→		qs.Set("limit", fmt.Sprintf("%d", query.MaxLines))
    58→	}

    66→	case QueryTypeRange:

    69→			qs.Set("end", strconv.FormatInt(query.End.UnixNano(), 10))
    70→			// NOTE: technically for streams-producing queries `step`
    71→			// is ignored, so it would be nicer to not send it in such cases,
    72→			// but we cannot detect that situation, so we always send it.
    73→			// it should not break anything.

    75→			//  a. Loki cannot

## Summary

I've found multiple Loki HTTP client implementations in the Grafana repository. Here are the most relevant findings:

### Primary HTTP Client Implementation for Loki Queries (TSDB)

**File Path:** `/workspace/grafana--26d36ec/pkg/tsdb/loki/api.go`

**Type:** `LokiAPI`

```go
type LokiAPI struct {
    client *http.Client
    url    string
    log    log.Logger
    tracer trace.Tracer
}
```

**Methods:**
- `DataQuery(ctx context.Context, query lokiQuery, responseOpts ResponseOpts) (*backend.DataResponse, error)` - Executes LogQL queries and returns data frames
- `RawQuery(ctx context.Context, resourcePath string) (RawLokiResponse, error)` - Executes raw HTTP requests to Loki endpoints

**Key Details:**
- This is the main HTTP client used by the Loki datasource plugin in Grafana
- It wraps the standard `*http.Client` for making requests to Loki API endpoints
- Supports both range queries (`/loki/api/v1/query_range`) and instant queries (`/loki/api/v1/query`)
- Handles query building, response parsing, and error handling
- Located in the `pkg/tsdb/loki` package (Time Series Database)
- Used by the `Service` struct in `/workspace/grafana--26d36ec/pkg/tsdb/loki/loki.go`

---

    34→func interpolateVariables(expr string, interval time.Duration, timeRange time.Duration, queryType dataquery.LokiQueryType, step time.Duration) string {
    35→	intervalText := gtime.FormatInterval(interval)
    36→	stepText := gtime.FormatInterval(step)
    37→	intervalMsText := strconv.FormatInt(int64(interval/time.Millisecond), 10)
    38→
    39→	rangeMs := timeRange.Milliseconds()
    40→	rangeSRounded := int64(math.Round(float64(rangeMs) / 1000.0))
    41→	rangeMsText := strconv.FormatInt(rangeMs, 10)
    42→	rangeSText := strconv.FormatInt(rangeSRounded, 10)
    43→
    44→	expr = strings.ReplaceAll(expr, varIntervalMs, intervalMsText)
    45→	expr = strings.ReplaceAll(expr, varInterval, intervalText)
    46→	expr = strings.ReplaceAll(expr, varRangeMs, rangeMsText)
    47→	expr = strings.ReplaceAll(expr, varRangeS, rangeSText)
    48→	ex

Based on my exploration of the workspace, I can provide you with information about where instant query requests are handled:

## Summary of Findings

The workspace contains the **Grafana repository** (not the standalone grafana-loki repository). The Grafana repository includes a Loki datasource plugin that handles requests to external Loki instances. Here are my findings:

### 1. **HTTP Handler for Instant Query Requests**

**File Path:** `/workspace/grafana--26d36ec/pkg/tsdb/loki/loki.go`

**Function Name:** `QueryData` (Lines 182-196)

**How it works:**
- The `QueryData` method on the `Service` struct handles incoming query requests
- It extracts datasource information, calls `queryData()` helper function
- The `queryData()` function parses the request using `parseQuery()` (from parse_query.go)
- For instant queries specifically, it calls `executeQuery()` which calls `runQuery()`
- `runQuery()` delegates to `api.DataQuery()` which constructs the HTTP request

### 2. **Query Parsing Logic**

**File Path:** `/workspace/grafana--26d36ec/pkg/tsdb/loki/parse_query.go`

**Key Functions:**
- `parseQuery()` (Lines 128-199) - Main parser that extracts query parameters
- `parseQueryType()` (Lines 67-83) - Determines if query is "instant" or "range"
- `interpolateVariables()` (Lines 34-65) - Handles variable substitution for instant queries

**Query Type Detection:**
```go
case "instant":
    return QueryTypeInstant, nil
case "range":
    return QueryTypeRange, nil
```

    53→	// and Loki does not like limit=0, even when it is not needed
    54→	// (for example for metric queries), so we
    55→	// only send it when it's set
    56→	if query.MaxLines > 0 {
    57→		qs.Set("limit", fmt.Sprintf("%d", query.MaxLines))
    58→	}

    21→	varRangeMs    = "$__range_ms"

    31→	// $__auto is a new variable and we don't want to support this templating format

    33→
    34→func interpolateVariables(expr string, interval time.Duration, timeRange time.Duration, queryType dataquery.LokiQueryType, step time.Duration) string {
    35→	intervalText := gtime.FormatInterval(interval)
    36→	stepText := gtime.FormatInterval(step)
    37→	intervalMsText := strconv.FormatInt(int64(interval/time.Millisecond), 10)
    38→
    39→	rangeMs := timeRange.Milliseconds()
    40→	rangeSRounded := int64(math.Round(float64(rangeMs) / 1000.0))
    41→	rangeMsText := strconv.FormatInt(rangeMs, 10)
    42→	rangeSText := strconv.FormatInt(rangeSRounded, 10)
    43→
    44→	expr = strings.ReplaceAll(expr, varIntervalMs, intervalMsText)
    45→	expr = strings.ReplaceAll(expr, varInterval, intervalText)
    46→	expr = strings.ReplaceAll(expr, varRangeMs, rangeMsText)
    47→	expr = strings.ReplaceAll(expr, varRangeS, rangeSText)
    48→	ex

# HTTP Handlers for Instant Query Endpoints in Loki

Based on the repository structure provided, the HTTP handlers for instant query endpoints like `/loki/api/v1/query` are located in **`pkg/querier/http.go`** (22,208 bytes).

This file is the primary handler for HTTP-based query requests in the Loki querier package. Additional related files that support query handling include:

- **`handler.go`** - Contains handler utilities (3,684 bytes)
- **`http_test.go`** - Comprehensive tests for HTTP functionality (25,372 bytes)

The `http.go` file works in conjunction with:
- **`querier.go`** - Core query logic (38,817 bytes)
- **`multi_tenant_querier.go`** - Multi-tenant query routing (14,816 bytes)

The `http_test.go` file provides extensive test coverage for the HTTP handlers, ensuring proper request handling and response formatting for instant query operations.

# Instant Query Handler Function

**Function Name:** `InstantQueryHandler`

**Location:** Approximately line 112-131 in the file

**Description:** This function handles incoming instant query HTTP requests. It validates that the query is a sample expression (metric query), checks entry limits, and executes the query using either the v2 engine (if available and data is recent enough) or falls back to the v1 engine.

The function signature is:
```go
func (q *QuerierAPI) InstantQueryHandler(ctx context.Context, req *queryrange.LokiInstantRequest) (logqlmodel.Result, error)
```

- **Fields:**

  - `url string` - The Loki server URL
  - `log log.Logger` - Logger instance
  - `tracer trace.Tracer` - OpenTelemetry tracer
- **Key Method:** `DataQuery()` (line 161) - Executes queries against Loki

### 2. **Instant Query Handler in grafana/loki** ✓
**Function:** `InstantQueryHandler`
- **File:** `pkg/querier/http.go`
- **Signature:** `func (q *QuerierAPI) InstantQueryHandler(ctx context.Context, req *queryrange.LokiInstantRequest) (logqlmodel.Result, error)`
- **Purpose:** Parses incoming HTTP instant query requests to `/loki/api/v1/query` endpoint

### 3. **API Call Chain**
1. Grafana datasource builds instant query request via `LokiAPI.DataQuery()`
2. `makeDataRequest()` constructs HTTP GET request to `/loki/api/v1/query` with query parameters
3. Loki server receives request and routes to `InstantQueryHandler()` 
4. Handler validates query and executes using query engine
5. Results returned to Grafana as JSON response
